Got it. Here’s one complete exercise, written cleanly and fully, ready to drop straight into a chapter or audiobook.

Box Breathing (4–4–4–4)
Find a comfortable position. You can sit upright or rest back—whatever lets your body feel supported. Let your shoulders drop. Let your jaw unclench. You don’t need to fix anything right now.
Your body has been carrying a lot. You’re allowed to pause.
This is Box Breathing, a simple, steady rhythm that helps your nervous system shift out of high alert and back into balance. We’ll breathe in four equal phases—like tracing the four sides of a box.
Here’s the pattern:
Inhale for 4
Hold for 4
Exhale for 4
Hold for 4
If four seconds feels too long, shorten it to three. If holding your breath feels uncomfortable today, soften the holds. There’s no wrong way to do this.
Let’s begin.
Breathe in through your nose for 1… 2… 3… 4 Hold gently for 1… 2… 3… 4 Exhale slowly through your mouth for 1… 2… 3… 4 Pause, empty, for 1… 2… 3… 4
Again.
Inhale 2… 3… 4 Hold 2… 3… 4 Exhale 2… 3… 4 Pause 2… 3… 4
As you continue, imagine tracing a square—each side even, steady, contained. Nothing rushed. Nothing forced.
Stay with this rhythm for 6 cycles, or about 3 minutes. If it feels supportive, you can continue up to 5 minutes.
If your mind wanders, that’s okay. Gently return to the count. The pattern does the work for you.
…
When you’re ready, let the structure fade. Allow your breath to return to its natural rhythm.
Notice what’s different now.
Maybe your chest feels softer. Maybe your thoughts feel less loud. Maybe there’s just a little more space.
This is something you created.
Box breathing works because equal, paced breathing signals safety to your nervous system. You didn’t remove the pressure in your life—you changed your relationship to it. That’s regulation. That’s skill.
You can use this anytime: Before a difficult conversation. When your thoughts start spiraling. When your body feels tense and alert for no clear reason.
Four sides. One box. A steady rhythm you can return to whenever you need grounding.
Take one last natural breath.
And continue on when you’re ready.

ChatGPT said:
Yep — you’re right. That version jumped straight into doing without first orienting the reader. Here’s a clean, complete version with a proper intro + explanation + the exercise, written in your grounded, teacher-voice style.

Box Breathing (4–4–4–4)
What this is
Box Breathing is a structured breathing technique that uses four equal phases—inhale, hold, exhale, hold—to create balance in the nervous system. It’s called “box” breathing because each breath traces the four equal sides of a square.
This pattern is commonly used by first responders, athletes, and people in high-pressure environments because it reliably brings the body out of fight-or-flight and back into a state of steadiness.
What matters here isn’t deep breathing or relaxation. What matters is pattern.
Your nervous system responds to rhythm. When the rhythm becomes even and predictable, your body gets the signal: I’m safe enough to settle.

Why this works
When stress is high, breathing becomes shallow and uneven. That keeps the body in alert mode.
Box Breathing does the opposite. The equal timing:
slows your heart rate
reduces stress arousal
activates the parasympathetic nervous system
You’re not forcing calm. You’re creating the conditions where calm can happen.

The practice
Find a comfortable position. You can sit upright or rest back—whatever allows your body to feel supported. Let your shoulders drop. Let your jaw soften.
You don’t need to change how you feel before you begin.
This breath will meet you exactly where you are.
We’ll breathe in four equal phases:
Inhale for 4
Hold for 4
Exhale for 4
Hold for 4
If four seconds feels too long, shorten it to three. If holding your breath feels uncomfortable today, soften the holds. There is no failing this practice.
Let’s begin.
Inhale through your nose for 1… 2… 3… 4 Hold gently for 1… 2… 3… 4 Exhale slowly through your mouth for 1… 2… 3… 4 Pause, empty, for 1… 2… 3… 4
Again.
Inhale 2… 3… 4 Hold 2… 3… 4 Exhale 2… 3… 4 Pause 2… 3… 4
As you continue, imagine tracing the four sides of a square—each side even, steady, contained.
Stay with this rhythm for 6 cycles, or about 3 minutes. If it feels supportive, you can continue up to 5 minutes.
If your mind wanders, gently return to the count. The pattern is doing the work.

Closing reflection
Now let the structure fade. Allow your breath to return to its natural rhythm.
Notice what’s different.
Maybe your chest feels softer. Maybe your thoughts feel less sharp. Maybe there’s simply more space than before.
You didn’t remove the pressure in your life. You changed your relationship to it.
This is what regulation feels like.
Box Breathing is a tool you can return to anytime—before a hard conversation, when your thoughts start spiraling, or when your body feels tense without a clear reason.
Four sides. One steady rhythm. A way back to yourself.

Just say the word.

Short answer: No — it’s not only breathing exercises. The JSON contains breathing exercises and many other types of practices.
What’s actually in the JSON
From the file contents, the exercises fall into multiple categories, not just breathwork

phoenix_raising_exercises
1. Breathing / Pranayama
Examples:
Box Breathing (4-4-4-4)
4-7-8 Breathing
Triangle Breathing
Coherence / Resonant Breathing
Alternate Nostril (Nadi Shodhana)
Ujjayi (Ocean Breath)
Sama Vritti (Equal Breathing)
Extended Exhale
Viloma (Interrupted Breath)
These are tagged like:


"category": "PRANAYAMA"

2. Somatic (non-breathing or breath-assisted body practices)
Examples:
Physiological Sigh (Release Breaths)
Progressive Muscle Relaxation
Body Scan Meditation
Lion’s Breath (expressive somatic release)
Grounding through the 5 Senses
Intention Breathing (hybrid somatic + cognitive)
Bee Breath (sound/vibration based)
These are tagged like:


"category": "SOMATIC"

Some use breath, but they are not pure breathing techniques — they involve:
muscle tension/release
sensory orientation
sound/vibration
attention scanning
emotional expression
3. Meditation / Compassion Practices
Examples:
Metta (Loving-Kindness)
Tonglen (Compassion Breathing)
These are contemplative practices, not regulation breathwork.

Bottom line
❌ It is not “only breathing exercises”
✅ It contains breathing + somatic + meditation practices
✅ There are dozens beyond basic breathwork (not just box breathing variants)
✅ Breath is often a carrier, not the core mechanism

Got it. Here is another exercise shown in full, verbatim in spirit and structure, with nothing skipped that would go into the script.
I’ll use Release Breaths (Physiological Sigh) because it’s clearly not box breathing and shows that the file contains non-box, non-purely-structured breathwork as well.

Release Breaths (Physiological Sigh)
Your body is holding all of this right now. You’re allowed to feel exactly this exhausted. You don’t have to perform having energy you don’t have.
And right here, in this moment, there’s something that can help.
Not by making everything disappear, but by giving your nervous system a way to remember it can settle.
I want to show you a breathing practice. It’s simple—your body already knows how to do this. We’re just going to work with it intentionally. Let’s practice together.
This is Release Breaths—also called physiological sighs. It’s one of the fastest ways to down-regulate your nervous system when you’re overwhelmed.
You’ll take a deep breath in, then let it all out with a full exhale— like a sigh of relief.
Find a position that feels comfortable right now. You can sit, stand, or lie down.
Let your shoulders drop away from your ears. Let your jaw soften—you might not have noticed it was clenched.
Let your body make sound if it wants to. The audible sigh is part of the release.
I’m going to step back now so you can practice at your own pace.
This practice is most effective when done for 1 to 2 minutes. That’s about 6 to 8 complete breath cycles.
When you’re ready to begin, pause and set a timer.
Follow the pattern:
Breathe in deeply… then exhale fully with a sigh—ahhhhh.
Repeat 6 to 8 times, or until your timer sounds.
When you’ve finished your practice— whether that’s one breath or eight— come back and continue. I’ll be here.
…
Welcome back.
Beautiful work.
Take a moment to notice how you feel now compared to when we began.
Notice the quality of your breath. The steadiness in your body.
This feeling— this is what you just created.
You just activated your body’s natural stress-release mechanism.
Sighing isn’t weakness. It’s biology.
Research from Stanford University shows that physiological sighs reset your breathing pattern when it becomes shallow or irregular during stress. Each sigh re-expands collapsed alveoli in your lungs and triggers a vagal response that calms your nervous system.
You didn’t just sigh. You physiologically interrupted the stress cycle your body was stuck in.
The deep inhale followed by the extended exhale activates your parasympathetic nervous system—your body’s natural calming mechanism.
You didn’t force anything. You didn’t willpower your way through.
You gave your nervous system permission to let go, and it did.
This tool is yours now.
The next time you feel that tightness building, that fog settling in, that exhaustion pressing down—
you can sigh. Intentionally.
Your body already knows this rhythm.
Notice what just happened in your body.
Your shoulders might be lower. Your breath might be deeper. Your chest might feel more open.
This is what release feels like.
You just gave your nervous system permission to reset.
Even if the external pressure hasn’t changed, something internal just did.
This is what self-regulation looks like— not eliminating the overwhelm, but changing your relationship to it.
And yet, the overwhelm is still real. The demands are still there.

contextualized
earned

Right now they are floating blocks with no narrative container.
This is not a formatting nit — it breaks therapeutic pacing and your validator intent.

2. Massive section ID reuse across chapters (semantic collision)
You are reusing the same Section IDs repeatedly across chapters, for example:


ch01_sec03
ch01_sec04
ch01_sec09
ch04_sec06

Across multiple chapters.
That causes:
❌ semantic flattening
❌ fingerprint clustering risk
❌ loss of chapter identity
❌ broken analytics (“what does ch01_sec03 mean anymore?”)
Even if text variants differ, structural sameness at the ID level is exactly what Phoenix Omega was designed to avoid.
Chapter ≠ shuffled deck of global sections
Each chapter should feel like a distinct arc, not a remix.

Example:

└─ Exercise: pra_box_4444_basic
Variant: 340w

Problems:
The integration text and the exercise text are not guaranteed to align
Integration should reference the exercise, not silently inject it
There’s no semantic handshake like:
“You’ll try this now”
“This is where we practice”
“Let’s apply what you just learned”
Right now it’s duct-taped, not integrated.

Issues:
Only 4 unique exercises in a 12-chapter long book
Two are repeated identically
No escalation, no modulation, no thematic mapping
This feels accidental, not designed.
If this were intentional, you’d expect:
early grounding
mid-book regulation
later autonomy or synthesis
Instead, it’s flat.

Some chapters have:
no exercise

There is no visible chapter contract.

The assembler is optimizing for section legality, not prose flow.
In other words:
“Is this section allowed here?” → ✅
“Does this form a readable chapter?” → ❌ not checked
Your basic prose template is not being enforced as a hard skeleton.

Chapter Prose Template

  ├─ Scene
  ├─ Insight

  └─ Exercise (embedded)

Now (actual behavior):


Chapter
  ├─ Section (any allowed type)

  ├─ Section (any allowed type)
  ├─ Optional exercise injection

So the system thinks:

That’s why you’re seeing:
exercise spam in some chapters
zero exercises in others

This is architecture drift, not a content bug.

❌ The engine ignores:
narrative buildup
thematic escalation

chapter-level promise
✅ The engine enforces:
section type legality
variant selection
count constraints
Humans don’t read in “sections.” They read in arcs.
You removed the arc governor.

That repetition is clearly not intentional prose design.
That happens because:
the same exercise prose is being injected
without checking whether it already exists in the chapter
or whether the surrounding narrative already introduced it
That’s not a writing issue. That’s missing de-duplication + missing prose awareness.

Your audit can say:

“Does the exercise feel earned?”
“Is the reader oriented?”
So you end up with something that is:
Structurally legal, experientially incoherent
That’s the worst failure mode.

7. The real diagnosis (no sugarcoating)
Phoenix Omega V4 currently assembles books the way a CMS assembles pages, not the way an author writes chapters.
You’ve accidentally built:
a section compositor instead of
a prose engine

8. What actually needs to change (high confidence)
You don’t need better writing. You need one hard rule restored:
The chapter prose template is non-negotiable.
Meaning:
A chapter is generated as one prose body
Sections are roles inside prose, not standalone blocks
Exercises are paragraph-level inserts, not sections
Repetition is controlled at the prose level, not the section level
Until that’s true, everything will feel “WTF” no matter how good the content is.

Fix A — Re-establish the Prose Spine (1 change)
Instead of:


Chapter
  ├─ Section
  ├─ Section
  ├─ Section

Do this:


ChapterProseTemplate
  ├─ slot: orientation
  ├─ slot: pattern
  ├─ slot: reframe
  ├─ slot: integration
  └─ slot: optional_exercise_insert

Sections fill slots, they do not become output units.
Output = single markdown string, not concatenated sections.

Fix B — Exercise becomes a callable insert, not a section
Change exercise handling to:

  prose += introduce_exercise()

{{ end }}

duplication
pacing
“WTF did this come from?” feeling

Instead of:

ch03::scene::f3

chapter_03.scene.primary.f3

Same content, zero collision, zero semantic drift.

Validator checks (binary pass/fail)
1. Prose continuity
No section headers mid-chapter
No abrupt voice resets
No “Here’s a practice” more than once
2. Exercise sanity
≤ 1 exercise per chapter
Exercise prose not duplicated elsewhere in chapter
Exercise preceded by explanatory paragraph
3. Arc completeness
Fail if missing:
orientation
reframe
integration
4. Duplication detector
Reject if any paragraph hash appears twice in same chapter
5. Read-aloud test (cheap but effective)
Sentence length variance exists
No more than N consecutive imperative sentences
No orphaned instructional blocks
If ANY fail → generation aborts
Not “warns”. Aborts.

1. Chapter Prose Contract (ONE PAGE)

# Chapter Prose Contract - Phoenix Omega V4

**Status:** ⚠️ **CURRENTLY VIOLATED**  
**Priority:** CRITICAL - NON-NEGOTIABLE

---

## The Contract

### A chapter **is prose**, not a container

* A chapter outputs **one continuous prose body**
* Sections are **semantic roles**, not standalone blocks
* The reader must be able to read start → end without feeling stitched

**If the chapter cannot be read aloud as a single, flowing piece of prose → FAIL**

---

## Required Chapter Arc (Minimum)

Every chapter must contain, in this order:

1. **Orientation** - Situational grounding (scene, question, or lived moment)
2. **Pattern Exposure** - What's happening beneath the surface
3. **Meaning / Reframe** - Why this pattern persists
4. **Integration** - What changes *in relationship*, not outcome
5. **Optional Practice** - Only if earned, introduced in prose, embedded not dropped in

---

## Exercises (Hard Rules)

* ❌ Exercises may NOT be top-level sections
* ❌ Exercises may NOT appear without narrative introduction
* ❌ Exercises may NOT repeat prose already used in the same chapter
* ✅ Exercises are **paragraph-level inserts**
* ✅ Max **1 exercise per chapter**
* ✅ Exercise prose must reference *this* chapter's insight

---

## Repetition Rules

* Intentional repetition = allowed
* Verbatim block repetition = forbidden
* "Here's a practice…" may appear **once per chapter, max**

---

## Identity Rules

* Section IDs are **chapter-scoped**
* ch01_sec03 cannot appear in Chapter 7
* Same *role* may recur; same *ID* may not

---

## Validation

A chapter is **invalid** if:
- ❌ It cannot be read as continuous prose
- ❌ Exercises appear as top-level sections
- ❌ Exercises lack narrative introduction
- ❌ Verbatim prose blocks repeat
- ❌ Section IDs cross chapter boundaries
- ❌ Chapter arc is incomplete

**This contract is non-negotiable. Violations = generation aborts.**

def validate_section_id_scope(section_id: str, chapter_num: int) -> bool:
    """Prevent ch01_sec03 from appearing in Chapter 7."""
    match = re.match(r'ch(\d+)_', section_id)
    if match:
        return int(match.group(1)) == chapter_num
    return True

4. Readability Validator
Create: phoenix_v4/validators/prose_readability_validator.py
class ProseReadabilityValidator:
    """Validates READABILITY, not just legality. ABORTS on failure."""
    
    def validate_chapter(self, content: str, chapter_num: int):
        failures = []
        
        # Check 1: Prose continuity
        if not self._check_prose_continuity(content):
            failures.append("Chapter lacks prose continuity")
        
        # Check 2: Exercise sanity (≤1, has intro)
        exercise_issues = self._check_exercise_sanity(content)
        failures.extend(exercise_issues)
        
        # Check 3: Arc completeness
        arc_issues = self._check_arc_completeness(content)
        failures.extend(arc_issues)
        
        # Check 4: Duplication
        if self._check_duplication(content):
            failures.append("Duplicate prose blocks detected")
        
        # Check 5: Read-aloud test
        read_aloud_issues = self._check_read_aloud(content)
        
        if failures:
            raise ValueError(f"Chapter {chapter_num} failed: {failures}")  # ABORT
class ProseReadabilityValidator:    """Validates READABILITY, not just legality. ABORTS on failure."""        def validate_chapter(self, content: str, chapter_num: int):        failures = []                # Check 1: Prose continuity        if not self._check_prose_continuity(content):            failures.append("Chapter lacks prose continuity")                # Check 2: Exercise sanity (≤1, has intro)        exercise_issues = self._check_exercise_sanity(content)        failures.extend(exercise_issues)                # Check 3: Arc completeness        arc_issues = self._check_arc_completeness(content)        failures.extend(arc_issues)                # Check 4: Duplication        if self._check_duplication(content):            failures.append("Duplicate prose blocks detected")                # Check 5: Read-aloud test        read_aloud_issues = self._check_read_aloud(content)                if failures:            raise ValueError(f"Chapter {chapter_num} failed: {failures}")  # ABORT

3️⃣ Golden invariant test (this can never regress again)

🔧 File: phoenix_v4/tests/test_prose_contract_invariants.py
✅ Test 1: No EXERCISE sections — ever


def test_no_exercise_sections_exist(book_plan):
    for chapter in book_plan.chapters:
        for section in chapter.sections:
            assert section.type != "EXERCISE", (
                f"INVALID: EXERCISE section found in Chapter {chapter.number}"
            )


✅ Test 2: Max one exercise per chapter


def test_max_one_exercise_per_chapter(book_plan):
    for chapter in book_plan.chapters:
        assert chapter.exercise_plan is None or isinstance(
            chapter.exercise_plan.exercise_id, str
        )

(You literally cannot have two if it’s not a list — that’s intentional.)

✅ PART 2 — 1-Page Architecture Truth Doc (Authoritative)

phoenix_v4/ARCHITECTURE_TRUTH.md


Contents (exact text, do not embellish)


# Phoenix Omega V4 — Architecture Truth

This document is authoritative.
If code contradicts this document, the code is wrong.

---

## Core Truth

Phoenix Omega V4 is a **prose-first book authoring system**.

It does NOT assemble books by concatenating sections.
It authors chapters as continuous prose.

---

## Chapter Authority

A chapter is a single, flowing prose body.

Sections are NOT output units.
Sections are semantic roles used to fill prose slots.

If a chapter cannot be read aloud without seams, it is invalid.

---

## Chapter Arc (Non-Negotiable)

Every chapter must contain, in order:

1. Orientation
2. Pattern Exposure
3. Meaning / Reframe
4. Integration
5. Optional Practice (at most one)

Missing any element = generation aborts.

---

## Exercises (Single Source of Truth)

EXERCISE IS NOT A SECTION.

Exercises may only exist in:

chapter.exercise_plan

Rules:
- Max 1 exercise per chapter
- Exercises are embedded in prose
- Exercises are introduced narratively
- Exercises are never standalone blocks

If section.type == EXERCISE → INVALID PLAN.

---

## Duplication Rules

Verbatim prose duplication is forbidden:
- Within a chapter
- Across chapters

Recognition is allowed.
Repetition is not.

---

## Validation Philosophy

Phoenix fails hard.

Invalid prose does not warn.
Invalid prose aborts generation.

If output exists, it has already passed all contracts.

---

## Non-Goals

Phoenix does not:
- Optimize for speed over quality
- Allow “mostly correct” output
- Defer authorial concerns to post-processing

---

## In Case of Confusion

If you are unsure how to implement something:

1. Preserve prose authority
2. Preserve chapter arc
3. Preserve single exercise rule

When in doubt, abort.

---

End of document.

You now have three locks:

CI lock — regressions cannot merge
And one human lock:
a truth doc that removes ambiguity
This is how systems stay correct at scale.

🎛️ STYLE-BALANCE CONSTRAINTS (Anti-Monotony Layer)

Rule
Constraint
Max repeats of same variant index
≤ 3 times per chapter
Consecutive repeats
≤ 2 in a row
Unique styles per chapter
≥ 3 distinct variants

2️⃣ Variant Selection Algorithm (Balanced)
Core idea
Instead of “pick blindly”, we bias against recently used variants.
Inputs
variants → {v1…v5}
base_seed → {book}:{chapter}:{section}
style_history → resolved variant indices so far in this chapter

🔧 PATCH — Prose Assembler (Exact Code)
File


phoenix_v4/assembler/prose_assembler.py

Add helper


def select_balanced_variant(
    variants: dict,
    seed: str,
    style_history: list[int],
) -> str:
    keys = sorted(variants.keys())  # ['v1'..'v5']
    indices = list(range(len(keys)))

    # Count usage
    usage = {i: style_history.count(i) for i in indices}

    # Enforce max-usage constraint (≤3)
    eligible = [
        i for i in indices
        if usage[i] < 3
    ]

    # Enforce no 3-in-a-row
    if len(style_history) >= 2 and style_history[-1] == style_history[-2]:
        eligible = [
            i for i in eligible
            if i != style_history[-1]
        ]

    if not eligible:
        raise ValueError("No eligible variant satisfies style-balance constraints")

    chosen = seeded_choice(seed, eligible)
    return keys[chosen], variants[keys[chosen]]["text"]


Use per section


variant_key, prose = select_balanced_variant(
    section.variants,
    seed=f"{book_seed}:{chapter_number}:{section_index}",
    style_history=chapter_style_history,
)

chapter_style_history.append(int(variant_key[1]))  # v3 → 3


3️⃣ Validator Add-On (Abort on Drift)
File


phoenix_v4/validators/prose_readability_validator.py

Add check


def _check_style_balance(self, style_history: list[int]):
    if len(set(style_history)) < 3:
        return ["Chapter uses fewer than 3 distinct style variants"]

    for i in range(len(style_history) - 2):
        if style_history[i] == style_history[i+1] == style_history[i+2]:
            return ["Three identical style variants in a row"]

    return []

Call it during chapter validation.

def test_style_balance(style_history):

            style_history[i+1] ==
            style_history[i+2]

🔧 PATCH — Book Context (Exact)
New file


phoenix_v4/assembler/book_context.py



class BookStyleContext:
    def __init__(self):
        self.chapter_styles = []   # list[list[int]]
        self.global_counts = {i: 0 for i in range(5)}

    def register_chapter(self, styles: list[int]):
        self.chapter_styles.append(styles)
        for s in styles:
            self.global_counts[s] += 1

    def dominant_style(self, chapter_styles: list[int]) -> int:
        return max(set(chapter_styles), key=chapter_styles.count)

    def validate_global_distribution(self):
        used = [k for k, v in self.global_counts.items() if v > 0]
        if len(used) < 4:
            raise ValueError("Book uses fewer than 4 of 5 style variants")

        total = sum(self.global_counts.values())
        for style, count in self.global_counts.items():
            if count / total > 0.40:
                raise ValueError(f"Style {style} dominates book ({count}/{total})")

File


phoenix_v4/assembler/assemble_v4.py

Initialize once


book_style_context = BookStyleContext()

After each chapter


book_style_context.register_chapter(chapter_style_history)

# Prevent dominant-style repetition
if len(book_style_context.chapter_styles) > 1:
    prev = book_style_context.dominant_style(
        book_style_context.chapter_styles[-2]
    )
    curr = book_style_context.dominant_style(
        chapter_style_history
    )
    if prev == curr:
        raise ValueError(
            f"Chapter {chapter_number} repeats dominant style {curr}"
        )

After book completion


book_style_context.validate_global_distribution()

🔧 PATCH — Arc Policy Object
New file


phoenix_v4/assembler/arc_policy.py



class ArcPolicy:
    OPENING = range(1, 4)
    MIDDLE = range(4, 9)
    CLOSING = range(9, 13)

    @staticmethod
    def allowed_variants(chapter_num: int):
        if chapter_num in ArcPolicy.OPENING:
            return {1, 2, 3, 4}
        if chapter_num in ArcPolicy.MIDDLE:
            return {1, 2, 3, 4, 5}
        if chapter_num in ArcPolicy.CLOSING:
            return {2, 3, 4, 5}
        return {1, 2, 3, 4, 5}

    @staticmethod
    def required_variants(chapter_num: int):
        if chapter_num in ArcPolicy.MIDDLE:
            return {3, 4}
        if chapter_num in ArcPolicy.CLOSING:
            return {4, 5}
        return set()

🔧 PATCH — Sameness Detector
New file


phoenix_v4/validators/sameness_detector.py



import hashlib

class SamenessDetector:
    def __init__(self):
        self.signatures = set()

    def fingerprint(self, text: str) -> str:
        lines = [l.strip() for l in text.splitlines() if l.strip()]
        first_phrases = [" ".join(l.split()[:6]) for l in lines[:5]]
        lengths = [len(l.split()) // 5 for l in lines[:5]]
        raw = "|".join(first_phrases + list(map(str, lengths)))
        return hashlib.md5(raw.encode()).hexdigest()

    def register(self, chapter_text: str, chapter_num: int):
        sig = self.fingerprint(chapter_text)
        if sig in self.signatures:
            raise ValueError(
                f"Chapter {chapter_num} fails sameness heuristic"
            )
        self.signatures.add(sig)


🔧 PATCH — Hook Into Assembly
File


phoenix_v4/assembler/assemble_v4.py

Initialize once:


sameness_detector = SamenessDetector()

After each chapter is assembled:


sameness_detector.register(chapter_prose, chapter_number)

    detector = SamenessDetector()
    for i, ch in enumerate(chapter_outputs, start=1):
        detector.register(ch, i)

1️⃣ Exact render_story() Stub (Authoritative)
This is pure wiring, not creative logic. It assumes story text is already finalized upstream (as you designed).
📄 File


phoenix_v4/assembler/story_renderer.py   (NEW)



def render_story(story_block: dict) -> str:
    """
    Render a chapter-opening story block into prose.

    story_block schema (already enforced upstream):
    {
        "role": "recognition" | "situational" | "lived_moment",
        "text": "<fully-formed prose string>"
    }
    """
    if not story_block:
        raise ValueError("render_story called with empty story_block")

    text = story_block.get("text")
    if not text or not text.strip():
        raise ValueError("Story block missing text")

    # Stories are prose, not headers or sections
    # Single blank line after to allow prose flow
    return text.strip() + "\n\n"


🔧 Wire it into assembly
📄 File


phoenix_v4/assembler/prose_assembler.py

At the very top of chapter assembly:

# --- Chapter open ---

if not opening_story:
    raise ValueError(f"Chapter {chapter_number} missing opening story")

chapter_paragraphs.append(render_story(opening_story))

This must execute before:
orientation
scene
hook
any other prose
That’s the entire fix.

## Chapter Opening Invariant (NON-NEGOTIABLE)

Every chapter MUST begin with exactly one story block.

🔒 Validator Enforcement
📄 File


phoenix_v4/validators/prose_readability_validator.py

Add:


def _check_story_first(self, content: str, chapter_num: int):
    first_paragraph = content.strip().split("\n\n", 1)[0]
    if not self._looks_like_story(first_paragraph):
        return [f"Chapter {chapter_num} does not open with a story"]
    return []

And call it during chapter validation.
You already have the story role metadata — this check is trivial.

def test_story_opens_each_chapter(chapter_outputs):
    for i, chapter in enumerate(chapter_outputs, start=1):
        first_block = chapter.strip().split("\n\n", 1)[0]
        assert looks_like_story(first_block), f"Chapter {i} missing opening story"

Box Breathing (4-4-4-4)
Your body is holding all of this right now. You're allowed to feel exactly this exhausted. You don't have to perform having energy you don't have. And right here, in this moment, there's something that can help. Not by making everything disappear, but by giving your nervous system a way to remember it can settle. I want to show you a breathing practice. It's simple—your body already knows how to do this. We're just going to work with it intentionally. Let's practice together.
This is Box Breathing. It's called that because each round has four equal sides: inhale, hold, exhale, hold. Four counts each. Like tracing the edges of a square.
Before we begin, just get comfortable. If you're sitting, let your feet touch the floor. If you're lying down, let your shoulders soften. Let your jaw unclench. You don't have to force calm. We're not chasing calm. We're just giving your body a structure it can trust.
If it feels okay, place one hand on your belly, or one hand on your chest—wherever you can feel your breath more clearly. If that feels weird, skip it. Just notice that you're breathing.
We're going to do six rounds.
Here we go.
Round one.
Inhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4. Exhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4.
Round two.
Inhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4. Exhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4.
Round three.
Inhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4. Exhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4.
Round four.
Inhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4. Exhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4.
Round five.
Inhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4. Exhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4.
Round six.
Inhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4. Exhale… 2… 3… 4. Hold… 2… 3… 4.
Now let the counting go.
Let your breathing return to its natural rhythm.
And just notice what changed.
Not “did the anxiety disappear.” Not “am I fixed.” Just this:
Is there even one percent more space inside your chest? One percent less pressure behind your eyes? One percent more room in your belly?
That is the point.
Because your nervous system doesn't need a lecture. It needs repetition of safety. It needs little proof moments that say: “I can come down.”
And every time you do this, you're teaching your body something important.
You're teaching it: “I can be here and still breathe.” “I can feel this and still come back.” “I can be stressed and still have a way through.”
If you want, do one more round on your own right now—slow and steady. Then continue your day with that tiny bit more space.

Story System Architecture - Phoenix Omega V4
Date: 2026-01-26
Status: ✅ AUTHORITATIVE REFERENCE
What This Document Is
This is the definitive specification for how the story system works in Phoenix Omega V4. It explains:
What the story system does
How stories flow from plan to prose
Where stories are injected
How chapter_open stories differ from other stories
The integration points and responsibilities
If code contradicts this document, the code is wrong.
Core Principle
Stories provide cognitive boundaries and emotional grounding.
Stories are not decorative. They are structural elements that:
Create chapter boundaries (felt, not just labeled)
Demonstrate patterns before explaining them
Show shifts and embodiment, not just describe them
Ground abstract teaching in lived experience
Story System Components
1. Story Planning (story_plan_v2)
Location: ChapterPlanV4.story_plan_v2
Structure:
StoryPlanV2(
    slot: str,              # "chapter_open" | "early" | "midpoint" | "pre_resolution" | "closing"
    role: str,              # "recognition" | "mechanism_proof" | "turning_point" | "embodiment"
    length: str,            # "micro" | "short" | "medium"
    engine: Optional[str],  # "false_alarm" | "avoidance_trap" | "waiting_room" | etc.
    story_asset_ref: Optional[str],  # Explicit story reference (if set, use this)
    character_id: Optional[str],      # For thread stories
    # ... other fields
)
StoryPlanV2(    slot: str,              # "chapter_open" | "early" | "midpoint" | "pre_resolution" | "closing"    role: str,              # "recognition" | "mechanism_proof" | "turning_point" | "embodiment"    length: str,            # "micro" | "short" | "medium"    engine: Optional[str],  # "false_alarm" | "avoidance_trap" | "waiting_room" | etc.    story_asset_ref: Optional[str],  # Explicit story reference (if set, use this)    character_id: Optional[str],      # For thread stories    # ... other fields)
Generated by: micro_story_planner.py::generate_story_plan_v2()
Contains: List of StoryPlanV2 objects, one per story slot used in the chapter.
2. Story Selection (StoryInjectorV4)
Location: phoenix_v4/assembler/story_injector_v4.py
Responsibility: Selects and loads story atoms deterministically.
Key Method:
select_micro_story(
    persona: str,
    topic: str,
    role: str,
    engine: Optional[str],
    length: str,
    book_seed: int,
    chapter: int,
    slot: str,
    used_story_ids: set,
    character_id: Optional[str]
) -> Optional[str]  # Returns story_id
select_micro_story(    persona: str,    topic: str,    role: str,    engine: Optional[str],    length: str,    book_seed: int,    chapter: int,    slot: str,    used_story_ids: set,    character_id: Optional[str]) -> Optional[str]  # Returns story_id
Process:
Lists available atoms from MicroStoryLoader
Filters out already-used stories
Selects deterministically via hash(book_seed, chapter, slot, role, engine)
Returns story_id (e.g., "gen_z_anxiety_false_alarm_recognition_micro_v03")
Guarantee: Same seed → same story selection forever.
3. Story Loading (MicroStoryLoader)
Location: phoenix_v4/libraries/micro_story_loader.py
Responsibility: Loads story atoms from filesystem.
Structure:
SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/story_bank/story_atoms/
  {persona}/
    {topic}/
      {engine}/
        {role}/
          {length}/
            *.txt  (story atom files)
            metadata.yaml
SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/story_bank/story_atoms/  {persona}/    {topic}/      {engine}/        {role}/          {length}/            *.txt  (story atom files)            metadata.yaml
Key Method:
load_atom(story_id: str) -> MicroStoryAtom
load_atom(story_id: str) -> MicroStoryAtom
Returns: MicroStoryAtom with text, persona, topic, role, engine, length, etc.
4. Story Wrapping (StoryWrapperLoader)
Location: phoenix_v4/libraries/story_wrapper_loader.py
Responsibility: Adds mode-appropriate intro/outro wrappers.
Wrappers provide:
Narrative transitions into/out of stories
Mode-specific framing (normal, teacher, teacher_composition, opinion)
Character name integration (for thread stories)
Key Method:
get_wrapper(engine, temperature, mode, type, variant, character_name) -> str
get_wrapper(engine, temperature, mode, type, variant, character_name) -> str
5. Story Injection (StoryInjectorV4.inject_micro_story())
Location: phoenix_v4/assembler/story_injector_v4.py
Responsibility: Injects wrapped story into content at specified position.
Key Method:
inject_micro_story(
    content: str,
    story_id: str,
    slot: str,
    mode: str,
    chapter: int,
    character_id: Optional[str],
    thread_id: Optional[str],
    thread_position: Optional[int],
    thread_total: Optional[int],
    position: str  # "after_para_2", "after_para_0", etc.
) -> str
inject_micro_story(    content: str,    story_id: str,    slot: str,    mode: str,    chapter: int,    character_id: Optional[str],    thread_id: Optional[str],    thread_position: Optional[int],    thread_total: Optional[int],    position: str  # "after_para_2", "after_para_0", etc.) -> str
Process:
Load atom via MicroStoryLoader
Get character info (if character_id provided)
Determine transition type (full, full_intro, full_outro, light_reentry)
Get wrappers via StoryWrapperLoader
Assemble: intro + story_text + outro
Inject into content at position
Returns: Content with story injected.
Story Slots and Roles
Slot Definitions
Slot	Timing	Function	Allowed Roles
chapter_open	Before any sections	Creates recognition, hooks listener	recognition
early	First third of chapter	Demonstrates pattern, builds case	recognition, mechanism_proof
midpoint	Middle of chapter	Shows shift beginning	turning_point, mechanism_proof
pre_resolution	Last third, before final teaching	Shows different action possible	embodiment, turning_point
closing	After final teaching, before chapter end	Lands the chapter, bridges to listener	embodiment
Role Definitions
Role	Purpose	When Used
recognition	"I see myself in this"	Opening, early
mechanism_proof	"This is how the pattern works"	Early, midpoint
turning_point	"Something shifted"	Midpoint, pre_resolution
embodiment	"This is possible"	Pre_resolution, closing
Story Flow: Plan → Prose
Step 1: Planning Phase
File: phoenix_v4/planning/micro_story_planner.py
Process:
generate_story_plan_v2() called during plan compilation
Determines which slots to use based on placement_policy (sparse, balanced, story_driven)
Creates StoryPlanV2 objects for each slot
Adds to ChapterPlanV4.story_plan_v2
Output: ChapterPlanV4 with story_plan_v2 populated.
Step 2: Assembly Phase
Two distinct paths:
Path A: chapter_open Stories (Chapter Level)
Location: phoenix_v4/assembler/prose_assembler.py
When: Before any sections are assembled.
Process:
assemble_prose() finds story_plan_v2 with slot="chapter_open"
Calls _load_story_text() which:
Uses section_assembler._story_injector (the story system we built)
Calls select_micro_story() to get story_id
Calls inject_micro_story() with empty content to get wrapped story text
Returns story text
Prepends story to chapter_paragraphs
Continues with section assembly
Result: Story appears before any section prose.
Path B: Other Stories (Section Level)
Location: phoenix_v4/assembler/section_assembler.py
When: During section assembly.
Process:
assemble_section() loops through chapter_plan.story_plan_v2
Skips chapter_open stories (handled at chapter level)
For other stories (early, midpoint, etc.):
Uses _story_injector.select_micro_story() to get story_id
Calls _story_injector.inject_micro_story() to inject into section content
Injects at position "after_para_2" (or other position)
Result: Story appears within section prose.
Critical Rules
Rule 1: chapter_open Stories Are Chapter-Level
❌ WRONG:
Injecting chapter_open stories into sections
Handling chapter_open at section level
✅ CORRECT:
chapter_open stories handled in prose_assembler.py
Appear before any sections
Use same story injector, but inject into empty content
Rule 2: Use the Story System We Built
❌ WRONG:
Creating new story injector instances
Duplicating story loading logic
Bypassing StoryInjectorV4 and MicroStoryLoader
✅ CORRECT:
Use section_assembler._story_injector (shared instance)
Use select_micro_story() for selection
Use inject_micro_story() for injection
Let the story system handle wrappers, character integration, etc.
Rule 3: Story Selection Is Deterministic
Guarantee: Same book_seed + same chapter + same slot + same role → same story_id
Implementation: Hash-based selection in MicroStoryLoader.select_atom_deterministically()
Consequence: Books are reproducible. Same seed → same book.
Rule 4: Stories Are Tracked for Uniqueness
Per-Book Tracking:
used_story_ids set prevents same story appearing twice in a book
Tracked in StoryInjectorV4._used_stories
Exception: chapter_open stories may reuse (they're chapter boundaries, not content)
Integration Points
Where Stories Are Handled
Component	Responsibility	Stories Handled
prose_assembler.py	Chapter-level story injection	chapter_open only
section_assembler.py	Section-level story injection	early, midpoint, pre_resolution, closing
story_injector_v4.py	Story selection and injection	All stories (via shared instance)
Story Injector Initialization
Location: section_assembler.py (lazy initialization)
When: First time a story needs to be injected
Shared: section_assembler._story_injector is used by both:
section_assembler.py (for section-level stories)
prose_assembler.py (for chapter_open stories)
Key Point: One story injector instance per assembler, shared across both assembly levels.

What the System Should Do (Summary)
Plan stories → micro_story_planner creates StoryPlanV2 objects
Select stories → StoryInjectorV4.select_micro_story() chooses atom deterministically
Load stories → MicroStoryLoader.load_atom() loads text from filesystem

Handle chapter_open specially → Injected at chapter level, before sections
Handle other stories normally → Injected at section level, within sections
What the System Should NOT Do
❌ Create duplicate story injectors

❌ Inject chapter_open into sections
❌ Handle stories inconsistently
❌ Break determinism

Below is a clean, enforceable property-test suite for book quality that:
does not rely on LLMs
does not rely on subjective judgment
runs in CI

Phoenix Omega V4 — Automatic Book Quality Property Tests
Goal: Guarantee that the generator cannot output a bad book.
These tests operate on generated output (book.md, audit_report.md, book_plan.yaml) and fail hard if any invariant is violated.

Test Group A — Structural Book Integrity
A1. Book Completeness Test
Property: All chapters must exist and be non-empty.


def test_all_chapters_present(book):
    assert len(book.chapters) == 12
    for ch in book.chapters:
        assert len(ch.text.strip()) > 500

Why: Prevents truncation bugs like the “only 4 chapters visible” incident.

A2. Chapter Order & Isolation
Property: Chapter boundaries are respected.


def test_chapter_boundaries(book):
    for i, ch in enumerate(book.chapters):
        assert f"CHAPTER {i+1}" in ch.header
        assert f"CHAPTER {i+2}" not in ch.text


Test Group B — Story Contract Enforcement
B1. Chapter-Open Story Exists
Property: Every chapter begins with a rendered chapter_open story.


def test_chapter_open_story(book):
    for ch in book.chapters:
        assert ch.text.lstrip().startswith(("When", "There was", "I remember", "You know that moment"))

1️⃣ Parsing the Book Into Chapters


import re
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import List

@dataclass
class Chapter:
    number: int
    header: str
    text: str


def parse_chapters(book_text: str) -> List[Chapter]:
    """
    Splits book text into chapters based on 'CHAPTER X' headers.
    """
    pattern = re.compile(r"(CHAPTER\s+\d+)", re.IGNORECASE)
    parts = pattern.split(book_text)

    chapters = []
    for i in range(1, len(parts), 2):
        header = parts[i].strip()
        body = parts[i + 1].strip()
        number = int(re.search(r"\d+", header).group())
        chapters.append(Chapter(number=number, header=header, text=body))

    return chapters


2️⃣ Story Detection (Wrapper-Based, Not Guessy)
This relies on your story wrapper intros, not vibes.


STORY_INTRO_PATTERNS = [
    r"\bwhen i was\b",
    r"\bi remember\b",
    r"\bthere was a moment\b",
    r"\byou know that moment\b",
    r"\bnot long ago\b",
    r"\bsomeone once\b",
]

STORY_OUTRO_PATTERNS = [
    r"\bthat moment stayed with me\b",
    r"\bthat was the first time\b",
    r"\bthat experience showed\b",
]


def find_story_blocks(text: str) -> List[str]:
    """
    Extracts story-like blocks using intro/outro heuristics.
    """
    paragraphs = [p.strip() for p in text.split("\n\n") if p.strip()]
    stories = []

    current = []
    in_story = False

    for p in paragraphs:
        if any(re.search(pat, p.lower()) for pat in STORY_INTRO_PATTERNS):
            current = [p]
            in_story = True
            continue

        if in_story:
            current.append(p)
            if any(re.search(pat, p.lower()) for pat in STORY_OUTRO_PATTERNS):
                stories.append("\n\n".join(current))
                current = []
                in_story = False

    return stories


def count_stories(text: str) -> int:
    return len(find_story_blocks(text))


3️⃣ Chapter-Open Story Detection
Chapter-open must be first meaningful prose, not buried.


def has_chapter_open_story(chapter: Chapter) -> bool:
    """
    Chapter-open story must appear within the first 3 paragraphs.
    """
    paragraphs = [p.strip() for p in chapter.text.split("\n\n") if p.strip()]
    opening = "\n\n".join(paragraphs[:3])
    return count_stories(opening) >= 1


4️⃣ Narrative Turn Detection (THIS IS IMPORTANT)
This checks for shift language, not just another story.


TURN_MARKERS = [
    r"\bbut then\b",
    r"\bsomething shifted\b",
    r"\bthat was the moment\b",
    r"\bi realized\b",
    r"\bwhat changed was\b",
    r"\bthat’s when\b",
]


def has_narrative_turn(chapter: Chapter) -> bool:
    """
    Detects a narrative turn anywhere after the opening third.
    """
    text = chapter.text.lower()
    cutoff = len(text) // 3
    later_text = text[cutoff:]

    return any(re.search(pat, later_text) for pat in TURN_MARKERS)


5️⃣ Embodiment Ending Detection (NOT Exposition)
This explicitly rejects teaching-style endings.


EXPOSITION_MARKERS = [
    r"\bthis means that\b",
    r"\bin summary\b",
    r"\bthe key takeaway\b",
    r"\bwhat you should do\b",
]

EMBODIMENT_MARKERS = [
    r"\byou can feel\b",
    r"\bnotice how\b",
    r"\blet yourself\b",
    r"\bstay with that\b",
    r"\bfor a moment\b",
]


def has_embodied_ending(chapter: Chapter) -> bool:
    """
    Last ~600 characters must feel embodied, not explanatory.
    """
    ending = chapter.text[-600:].lower()

    if any(re.search(pat, ending) for pat in EXPOSITION_MARKERS):
        return False

    return any(re.search(pat, ending) for pat in EMBODIMENT_MARKERS)


6️⃣ Arc Order Validation
This enforces Orientation → Pattern → Reframe → Integration.


ARC_MARKERS = {
    "orientation": [r"\byou might\b", r"\bimagine\b", r"\bpicture this\b"],
    "pattern": [r"\bthis keeps happening\b", r"\bthe pattern is\b"],
    "reframe": [r"\bwhat’s actually happening\b", r"\bthis isn’t about\b"],
    "integration": [r"\bso now\b", r"\bfrom here\b", r"\byou don’t need to\b"],
}


def detect_arc_positions(text: str):
    positions = {}
    lower = text.lower()

    for stage, patterns in ARC_MARKERS.items():
        for pat in patterns:
            m = re.search(pat, lower)
            if m:
                positions[stage] = m.start()
                break

    return positions


def arc_is_valid(chapter: Chapter) -> bool:
    pos = detect_arc_positions(chapter.text)
    required = ["orientation", "pattern", "reframe", "integration"]

    if not all(k in pos for k in required):
        return False

    return (
        pos["orientation"]
        < pos["pattern"]
        < pos["reframe"]
        < pos["integration"]
    )


7️⃣ Cross-Chapter Similarity Guard (Lightweight, Fast)


from sklearn.feature_extraction.text import TfidfVectorizer
from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import cosine_similarity


def chapters_too_similar(ch1: Chapter, ch2: Chapter, threshold=0.82) -> bool:
    vec = TfidfVectorizer(stop_words="english", max_features=500)
    X = vec.fit_transform([ch1.text, ch2.text])
    sim = cosine_similarity(X)[0, 1]
    return sim >= threshold


8️⃣ Putting It Together (One Call)


def chapter_passes_quality(chapter: Chapter) -> bool:
    return (
        has_chapter_open_story(chapter)
        and count_stories(chapter.text) >= 2
        and has_narrative_turn(chapter)
        and has_embodied_ending(chapter)
        and arc_is_valid(chapter)
    )

B. BookQualityGate implementation


from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import List

from phoenix_v4.validators.story_wrapper_signatures import (
    STORY_OPEN_MARKERS,
    STORY_CLOSE_MARKERS,
)
from phoenix_v4.validators.turn_signatures import TURN_MARKERS


@dataclass
class ChapterResult:
    number: int
    passed: bool
    errors: List[str]


class BookQualityGate:
    """
    Authoritative, hard-fail validator.
    If this fails, generation MUST abort.
    """

    def validate_book(self, book_text: str) -> None:
        chapters = self._parse_chapters(book_text)

        failures = []
        for ch in chapters:
            result = self._validate_chapter(ch["number"], ch["text"])
            if not result.passed:
                failures.append(result)

        if failures:
            error_report = "\n\n".join(
                self._format_failure(f) for f in failures
            )
            raise RuntimeError(
                "BOOK QUALITY GATE FAILED\n\n" + error_report
            )

    # ---------- Chapter-level ----------

    def _validate_chapter(self, number: int, text: str) -> ChapterResult:
        errors = []

        if not self._has_chapter_open_story(text):
            errors.append("Missing chapter_open story")

        if not self._has_midpoint_story(text):
            errors.append("Missing midpoint story")

        if not self._has_narrative_turn(text):
            errors.append("Missing narrative turn")

        if not self._has_embodied_ending(text):
            errors.append("Ending is not embodied")

        return ChapterResult(
            number=number,
            passed=len(errors) == 0,
            errors=errors,
        )

    # ---------- Atomic checks ----------

    def _has_chapter_open_story(self, text: str) -> bool:
        paragraphs = self._paragraphs(text)
        return any(
            p.startswith(tuple(STORY_OPEN_MARKERS))
            for p in paragraphs[:5]
        )

    def _has_midpoint_story(self, text: str) -> bool:
        paragraphs = self._paragraphs(text)
        midpoint = paragraphs[len(paragraphs) // 3 : 2 * len(paragraphs) // 3]
        return any(
            p.startswith(tuple(STORY_OPEN_MARKERS))
            for p in midpoint
        )

    def _has_narrative_turn(self, text: str) -> bool:
        lower = text.lower()
        return any(marker in lower for marker in TURN_MARKERS)

    def _has_embodied_ending(self, text: str) -> bool:
        ending = text[-700:].lower()

        forbidden = [
            "in summary",
            "the key takeaway",
            "this means that",
            "what you should do",
        ]
        required = [
            "notice how",
            "let yourself",
            "stay with that",
            "you can feel",
        ]

        if any(f in ending for f in forbidden):
            return False

        return any(r in ending for r in required)

    # ---------- Helpers ----------

    def _parse_chapters(self, book_text: str):
        chapters = []
        current = []
        number = 0

        for line in book_text.splitlines():
            if line.startswith("# Chapter"):
                if current:
                    chapters.append({
                        "number": number,
                        "text": "\n".join(current),
                    })
                number += 1
                current = [line]
            else:
                current.append(line)

        if current:
            chapters.append({
                "number": number,
                "text": "\n".join(current),
            })

        return chapters

    def _paragraphs(self, text: str):
        return [p.strip() for p in text.split("\n\n") if p.strip()]

    def _format_failure(self, result: ChapterResult) -> str:
        return (
            f"Chapter {result.number} FAILED:\n"
            + "\n".join(f" - {e}" for e in result.errors)
        )

from phoenix_v4.libraries.micro_story_loader import MicroStoryLoader
from phoenix_v4.planning.format_plan_compiler import compile_format_plan

    format_type='standard_book',
    persona='gen_z_professionals',
    topic='anxiety',
    locale='los_angeles',
    book_size='long',
    teacher_mode='off',
    seed='101',
)

loader = MicroStoryLoader(atoms_root) if atoms_root.exists() else None

missing = []
available = []

for ch in plan.chapters:
    if hasattr(ch, 'story_plan_v2') and ch.story_plan_v2:
        for story_plan in ch.story_plan_v2:
            role = getattr(story_plan, 'role', 'unknown')
            engine = getattr(story_plan, 'engine', None)
            slot = getattr(story_plan, 'slot', 'unknown')
            
            if loader:
                # Check if atoms exist
                atoms = loader.list_atoms(
                    persona='gen_z_professionals',
                    topic='anxiety',
                    engine=engine,
                    role=role,
                    length='micro'
                )
                
                if atoms:
                    available.append((role, engine, slot, ch.chapter, len(atoms)))
                else:
                    missing.append((role, engine, slot, ch.chapter))
            else:
                missing.append((role, engine, slot, ch.chapter))

print(f'Available: {len(available)}')
print(f'Missing: {len(missing)}')
print()
print('MISSING STORIES:')
for role, engine, slot, chapter in missing:

# Create a simple gap analysis
from pathlib import Path
from phoenix_v4.libraries.micro_story_loader import MicroStoryLoader
from phoenix_v4.planning.format_plan_compiler import compile_format_plan

plan = compile_format_plan(
    format_type='standard_book',
    persona='gen_z_professionals',
    topic='anxiety',
    locale='los_angeles',
    book_size='long',
    teacher_mode='off',
    seed='101',
)

atoms_root = Path('SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/story_bank/story_atoms')
loader = MicroStoryLoader(atoms_root) if atoms_root.exists() else None

# Collect needed stories
needed = {}
missing = {}

for ch in plan.chapters:
    if hasattr(ch, 'story_plan_v2') and ch.story_plan_v2:
        for story_plan in ch.story_plan_v2:
            role = getattr(story_plan, 'role', 'unknown')
            engine = getattr(story_plan, 'engine', None) or 'any'
            slot = getattr(story_plan, 'slot', 'unknown')
            
            key = f'{role}/{engine}'
            if key not in needed:
                needed[key] = []
            needed[key].append((ch.chapter, slot))
            
            if loader:
                atoms = loader.list_atoms(
                    persona='gen_z_professionals',
                    topic='anxiety',
                    engine=engine if engine != 'any' else None,
                    role=role,
                    length='micro'
                )
                if not atoms:
                    if key not in missing:
                        missing[key] = []
                    missing[key].append((ch.chapter, slot))

print('=== STORY GAP ANALYSIS ===')
print(f'Persona: gen_z_professionals')
print(f'Topic: anxiety')
print()
print(f'Total story slots needed: {sum(len(v) for v in needed.values())}')
print(f'Missing story slots: {sum(len(v) for v in missing.values())}')
print()
if missing:
    print('MISSING STORIES:')
    for key in sorted(missing.keys()):
        role, engine = key.split('/')
        chapters = [f'ch{c}' for c, s in missing[key]]
        print(f'  {role}/{engine}: needed in {chapters}')
        print(f'    Command to generate:')
        print(f'      python3 tools/generate_story_prompts.py --persona gen_z_professionals --topic anxiety --role {role} --engine {engine} --length micro')
"

# Final gap analysis with actionable output
from pathlib import Path
from phoenix_v4.libraries.micro_story_loader import MicroStoryLoader
from phoenix_v4.planning.format_plan_compiler import compile_format_plan

plan = compile_format_plan(
    format_type='standard_book',
    persona='gen_z_professionals',
    topic='anxiety',
    locale='los_angeles',
    book_size='long',
    teacher_mode='off',
    seed='101',
)

atoms_root = Path('SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/story_bank/story_atoms')
loader = MicroStoryLoader(atoms_root) if atoms_root.exists() else None

# Collect needed stories
needed = {}
missing = {}
available = {}

for ch in plan.chapters:
    if hasattr(ch, 'story_plan_v2') and ch.story_plan_v2:
        for story_plan in ch.story_plan_v2:
            role = getattr(story_plan, 'role', 'unknown')
            engine = getattr(story_plan, 'engine', None) or 'any'
            slot = getattr(story_plan, 'slot', 'unknown')
            
            key = f'{role}/{engine}'
            if key not in needed:
                needed[key] = []
            needed[key].append((ch.chapter, slot))
            
            if loader:
                # Try with specific engine first
                atoms = loader.list_atoms(
                    persona='gen_z_professionals',
                    topic='anxiety',
                    engine=engine if engine != 'any' else None,
                    role=role,
                    length='micro'
                )
                if atoms:
                    if key not in available:
                        available[key] = []
                    available[key].append((ch.chapter, slot, len(atoms)))
                else:
                    if key not in missing:
                        missing[key] = []
                    missing[key].append((ch.chapter, slot))

print('=== STORY GAP ANALYSIS ===')
print(f'Persona: gen_z_professionals')
print(f'Topic: anxiety')
print()
print(f'Total story slots needed: {sum(len(v) for v in needed.values())}')
print(f'Available: {sum(len(v) for v in available.values())}')
print(f'Missing: {sum(len(v) for v in missing.values())}')
print()
if missing:
    print('MISSING STORIES (by role/engine):')
    for key in sorted(missing.keys()):
        role, engine = key.split('/')
        chapters = sorted(set([c for c, s in missing[key]]))
        slots = sorted(set([s for c, s in missing[key]]))
        print(f'  {role}/{engine}:')
        print(f'    Needed in chapters: {chapters}')
        print(f'    Slots: {slots}')
        print(f'    Generate with:')
        print(f'      python3 tools/generate_story_prompts.py --persona gen_z_professionals --topic anxiety --role {role} --engine {engine} --length micro')
        print()

# The real issue: when engine=None, list_atoms needs to search all engines
from pathlib import Path
from phoenix_v4.libraries.micro_story_loader import MicroStoryLoader

atoms_root = Path('SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/story_bank/story_atoms')
loader = MicroStoryLoader(atoms_root) if atoms_root.exists() else None

if loader:
    persona = 'gen_z_professionals'
    topic = 'anxiety'
    role = 'turning_point'
    
    # When engine=None, we need to search all engines
    engines = ['watcher', 'waiting_room', 'safety_ritual', 'false_alarm', 'spiral', 'avoidance_trap']
    all_atoms = []
    
    print('turning_point stories across all engines (micro):')
    for engine in engines:
        atoms = loader.list_atoms(persona, topic, engine=engine, role=role, length='micro')
        if atoms:
            all_atoms.extend(atoms)
            print(f'  {engine}: {len(atoms)} atoms')
    
    if not all_atoms:
        print('  Trying fallback lengths...')
        for engine in engines:
            for fallback in ['cool', 'warm']:
                atoms = loader.list_atoms(persona, topic, engine=engine, role=role, length=fallback)
                if atoms:
                    all_atoms.extend(atoms)
                    print(f'  {engine}/{fallback}: {len(atoms)} atoms')
                    break
    
    print(f'Total available: {len(all_atoms)} atoms')
    print()
    print('ISSUE: When engine=None, list_atoms() only searches exact match.')
    print('SOLUTION: Either generate micro length stories OR fix list_atoms to search all engines when engine=None')
"

# Final analysis: what's the actual problem?
from pathlib import Path
from phoenix_v4.libraries.micro_story_loader import MicroStoryLoader
from phoenix_v4.planning.format_plan_compiler import compile_format_plan

plan = compile_format_plan(
    format_type='standard_book',
    persona='gen_z_professionals',
    topic='anxiety',
    locale='los_angeles',
    book_size='long',
    teacher_mode='off',
    seed='101',
)

atoms_root = Path('SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/story_bank/story_atoms')
loader = MicroStoryLoader(atoms_root) if atoms_root.exists() else None

print('=== ROOT CAUSE ANALYSIS ===')
print()

# Check what stories are planned
for ch in plan.chapters:
    if hasattr(ch, 'story_plan_v2') and ch.story_plan_v2:
        for story_plan in ch.story_plan_v2:
            role = getattr(story_plan, 'role', 'unknown')
            engine = getattr(story_plan, 'engine', None)
            slot = getattr(story_plan, 'slot', 'unknown')
            length = getattr(story_plan, 'length', 'micro')
            
            if loader and role == 'turning_point' and slot == 'midpoint':
                # Check what's available
                atoms_micro = loader.list_atoms('gen_z_professionals', 'anxiety', engine=engine, role=role, length='micro')
                atoms_cool = loader.list_atoms('gen_z_professionals', 'anxiety', engine=engine, role=role, length='cool') if not atoms_micro else []
                atoms_warm = loader.list_atoms('gen_z_professionals', 'anxiety', engine=engine, role=role, length='warm') if not atoms_micro else []
                
                if not atoms_micro and not atoms_cool and not atoms_warm:
                    print(f'Chapter {ch.chapter}: {role}/{engine}/{length} - COMPLETELY MISSING')
                elif not atoms_micro:
                    print(f'Chapter {ch.chapter}: {role}/{engine} - micro MISSING (but cool/warm exist)')
                    print(f'  Available: cool={len(atoms_cool)}, warm={len(atoms_warm)}')
                    print(f'  FIX: System should use fallback lengths (already implemented)')
                    print(f'  OR: Generate micro length stories')
                    break

print()
print('=== SOLUTION OPTIONS ===')
print()
print('Option 1: Generate missing micro length stories')
print('  - turning_point role needs micro length stories')
print('  - Currently only cool/warm exist')
print('  - Generate with:')
print('    python3 tools/generate_story_prompts.py --persona gen_z_professionals --topic anxiety --role turning_point --engine watcher --length micro')
print()
print('Option 2: Fix fallback logic (if not working)')
print('  - System should fallback from micro -> cool/warm')
print('  - Check if fallback is working correctly')

story_loader = StoryLoader(story_bank_path) if story_bank_path.exists() else None

if loader and story_loader:
    injector = StoryInjectorV4(story_loader, micro_story_loader=loader)
    
    # Try to select a turning_point story (should use fallback)
    story_id = injector.select_micro_story(
        persona='gen_z_professionals',
        topic='anxiety',
        role='turning_point',
        engine=None,  # any engine
        length='micro',
        book_seed=101,
        chapter=1,
        slot='midpoint',
        used_story_ids=set(),
    )
    
    if story_id:
        print(f'✅ Story found: {story_id}')
        print('   Fallback logic is working')
    else:
        print('❌ No story found')
        print('   Fallback logic may not be working when engine=None')
        print()

        # Check all engines
        for engine in ['watcher', 'waiting_room', 'safety_ritual', 'false_alarm', 'spiral', 'avoidance_trap']:
            atoms = loader.list_atoms('gen_z_professionals', 'anxiety', engine=engine, role='turning_point', length='cool')

# The issue: when engine=None, list_atoms doesn't search all engines
from pathlib import Path
from phoenix_v4.libraries.micro_story_loader import MicroStoryLoader

atoms_root = Path('SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/story_bank/story_atoms')
loader = MicroStoryLoader(atoms_root) if atoms_root.exists() else None

if loader:
    # When engine=None, list_atoms only matches atoms where engine is None
    # But atoms have specific engines (watcher, waiting_room, etc.)
    # So engine=None won't match anything
    
    atoms_none = loader.list_atoms('gen_z_professionals', 'anxiety', engine=None, role='turning_point', length='micro')
    print(f'With engine=None: {len(atoms_none)} atoms')
    
    # Need to search all engines
    all_engines = ['watcher', 'waiting_room', 'safety_ritual', 'false_alarm', 'spiral', 'avoidance_trap']
    total = 0
    for engine in all_engines:
        atoms = loader.list_atoms('gen_z_professionals', 'anxiety', engine=engine, role='turning_point', length='cool')
        total += len(atoms)

Fixing the issue where engine=None doesn't search across all engines.
The Problem:
When engine=None is passed to select_micro_story, it calls list_atoms(persona, topic, None, role, length). The list_atoms method in MicroStoryLoader only returns atoms where the engine metadata field is explicitly None, not atoms from all engines (like watcher, waiting_room, etc.).
The Fix Needed:
When engine=None, I need to:
Discover all available engines for the persona/topic combination
Search each engine individually
Aggregate the results
Apply the same fallback length logic across all engines
What I'm Stuck On:

Should I:
Write the complete replacement code now?
Or would you prefer a different approach to discover available engines?
The goal is to ensure that when the story plan requests engine=None (meaning "any engine"), the system searches across all available engines, not just atoms with engine=None in their metadata.

🔧 Correct behavior (pseudo-code, final)


def _collect_candidate_atoms(
    self,
    persona,
    topic,
    role,
    engine,
    length,
):
    candidates = []

    # Case 1: engine explicitly specified → current behavior
    if engine is not None:
        candidates.extend(
            self.micro_story_loader.list_atoms(
                persona=persona,
                topic=topic,
                engine=engine,
                role=role,
                length=length,
            )
        )
        return candidates

    # Case 2: engine=None → search ALL engines
    engines = self.micro_story_loader.list_engines(
        persona=persona,
        topic=topic,
    )

    for eng in engines:
        candidates.extend(
            self.micro_story_loader.list_atoms(
                persona=persona,
                topic=topic,
                engine=eng,
                role=role,
                length=length,
            )
        )

    return candidates

Then apply the existing fallback length logic (micro → cool → warm) on the aggregated candidate set, not per-engine.
No new APIs required beyond a simple list_engines() helper (which can be filesystem-based).

🔧 What this fixes permanently
❌ No false “content gap” claims
❌ No need to generate duplicate micro stories
❌ No lenient duplication hacks
✅ Planner semantics are respected
✅ Determinism preserved
✅ BookQualityGate failures become real failures

#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Generate a test book and audit for QA."""

import sys
from pathlib import Path

# Add project root to path
repo_root = Path(__file__).parent
sys.path.insert(0, str(repo_root))

from phoenix_ui import actions
from phoenix_v4.tools.book_audit import AuditAssembler, generate_audit_report

def main():
    print("📚 Generating test book...")
    print("   Persona: gen_z_professionals")
    print("   Topic: anxiety")
    print("   Chapters: 12")
    print("   Duration: 30 minutes")
    print()
    
    # Generate book
    result = actions.action_build_manifest(
        topic='anxiety',
        persona='gen_z_professionals',
        beat_map=None,
        book_arc=None,
        chapters=12,
        duration_minutes=30,
        book_seed=None,  # Random seed
    )
    
    if result['status'] != 'success':
        print(f"❌ Book generation failed: {result.get('error', 'Unknown error')}")
        return 1
    
    manifest_path = Path(result['manifest_path'])
    plan_path = manifest_path.parent / f"{manifest_path.stem}_plan.yaml"
    
    if not plan_path.exists():
        print(f"❌ Plan file not found: {plan_path}")
        return 1
    
    print(f"✅ Book generated: {manifest_path}")
    print(f"📋 Plan file: {plan_path}")
    print()
    
    # Find sections library
    sections_lib = repo_root / "SOURCE_OF_TRUTH" / "data" / "sections_library"
    if not sections_lib.exists():
        print(f"❌ Sections library not found: {sections_lib}")
        return 1
    
    # Run audit
    print("📊 Running audit...")
    auditor = AuditAssembler(sections_lib)
    audit = auditor.audit_book(plan_path)
    report = generate_audit_report(audit)
    
    # Save audit report
    audit_path = manifest_path.parent / f"{manifest_path.stem}_audit.txt"
    with open(audit_path, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
        f.write(report)
    
    print(f"✅ Audit report saved: {audit_path}")
    print()
    print("=" * 80)
    print("AUDIT SUMMARY")
    print("=" * 80)
    print(report)
    print("=" * 80)
    print()
    print(f"📁 Files generated:")
    print(f"   - Manifest: {manifest_path}")
    print(f"   - Plan: {plan_path}")
    print(f"   - Audit: {audit_path}")
    
    # Try to find book.md if it exists
    book_md = manifest_path.parent / f"{manifest_path.stem}.md"
    if book_md.exists():
        print(f"   - Book: {book_md}")
    
    return 0

if __name__ == "__main__":
    sys.exit(main())

✅ Required core algorithm (pseudocode)


for chapter in book:
    assembled_sections = []

    for slot in chapter_template.slots:
        variant = choose_variant(
            slot_id=slot.slot_id,
            variants=slot.variants,
            seed=book_seed,
            chapter_index=chapter.index
        )

        section_text = render(slot_id=slot.slot_id, variant=variant)

        assembled_sections.append(section_text)

    chapter_text = stitch_in_order(assembled_sections)

## Step 4: Explicit Bans (PR Rejection Criteria)

**If I see ANY of these patterns in the chapter assembly path, the PR is rejected:**

### ❌ Banned Patterns

1. **Section Pooling**
   - ❌ "Pick any section from SCENE pool"
   - ❌ "Select section matching role HOOK"
   - ❌ "Choose from available sections"
   - ❌ Global section pools shared across slots

2. **Fallback Logic**
   - ❌ "If v1 missing, try v2"
   - ❌ "If slot fails, substitute with another slot"
   - ❌ "If section not found, use default"
   - ❌ Any except block that continues assembly after slot failure

3. **Validator-Driven Recovery**
   - ❌ "Validator will fix it later"
   - ❌ "Post-processing will adjust"
   - ❌ "Validation catches errors and recovers"
   - Validators may **check**, they may not **decide** outcomes

4. **Variable Section Counts**
   - ❌ "Sometimes 8 sections, sometimes 12"
   - ❌ "Min 6, max 14 sections per chapter"
   - ❌ Dynamic section counts based on content availability

5. **Cross-Slot Substitution**
   - ❌ "slot_01 can use slot_02 content if needed"
   - ❌ "Any OPEN section works for slot_01"
   - ❌ Slot content shared across different slot positions

### ✅ Required Patterns

1. **Fixed Slot Order**
   - ✅ Exactly 10 slots per chapter (positions 1-10)
   - ✅ Slots always in same order: slot_01_open → slot_10_takeaway

2. **Deterministic Selection**
   - ✅ choose_variant(slot_id, variants, seed, chapter_index) returns same variant for same inputs
   - ✅ No randomness, no heuristics, no style balancing

3. **Hard Abort on Failure**
   - ✅ Missing variant → SlotAssemblyError raised immediately
   - ✅ Missing section content → SlotAssemblyError raised immediately
   - ✅ Render failure → SlotAssemblyError raised immediately
   - ✅ No recovery, no substitution, no fallback

---

Guardrail tests for slot-based assembly.

These tests ensure banned patterns do not appear in assembly code.

import re
from pathlib import Path
import pytest

# Banned patterns that must NOT appear in assembly code
BANNED_PATTERNS = [
    r"\bpool\b",
    r"\bfallback\b",
    r"\bsubstitute\b",
    r"\brecovery\b",
    r"pick any section",
    r"match role",
    r"select from available",
    r"try another",
    r"if missing, use",
    r"validator will fix",
    r"post-process",
    r"section pool",
    r"role pool",
    r"available sections",
    r"fallback to",
    r"substitute with",
    r"recover from",
]

# Files to check
ASSEMBLY_FILES = [
    "phoenix_v4/assembler/slot_assembler.py",
    "phoenix_v4/assembler/assemble_v4.py",
]


def test_no_banned_patterns_in_assembly():
    """Fail if banned patterns appear in assembly code."""
    repo_root = Path(__file__).parent.parent.parent
    
    violations = []
    
    for file_path in ASSEMBLY_FILES:
        full_path = repo_root / file_path
        
        # Skip if file doesn't exist (e.g., slot_assembler.py not yet created)
        if not full_path.exists():
            continue
        
        content = full_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
        content_lower = content.lower()
        
        for pattern in BANNED_PATTERNS:
            # Use case-insensitive search
            matches = re.finditer(pattern, content_lower, re.IGNORECASE)
            for match in matches:
                # Get line number
                line_num = content[:match.start()].count("\n") + 1
                line_content = content.split("\n")[line_num - 1].strip()
                
                violations.append({
                    "file": file_path,
                    "line": line_num,
                    "pattern": pattern,
                    "context": line_content[:100],
                })
    
    if violations:
        error_msg = "Banned patterns found in assembly code:\n\n"
        for v in violations:
            error_msg += f"  {v['file']}:{v['line']} - Pattern '{v['pattern']}'\n"
            error_msg += f"    Context: {v['context']}\n\n"
        
        error_msg += "\nThese patterns indicate pool-based or fallback logic.\n"
        error_msg += "Slot-based assembly must not use these patterns."
        
        pytest.fail(error_msg)
    
    # Test passes if no violations found
    assert True


def test_slot_assembler_exists():
    """Verify slot assembler file exists (if architecture decision is YES)."""
    repo_root = Path(__file__).parent.parent.parent
    slot_assembler_path = repo_root / "phoenix_v4" / "assembler" / "slot_assembler.py"
    
    # This test will fail if slot assembler doesn't exist
    # (Only run this after architecture decision is YES)
    if not slot_assembler_path.exists():
        pytest.skip(
            "slot_assembler.py not found. "
            "This test should pass after slot-based assembler is implemented."
        )
    
    # If file exists, verify it has required functions
    content = slot_assembler_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
    
    required_functions = [
        "choose_variant",
        "render_slot_content",
        "assemble_chapter_slots",
    ]
    
    missing = []
    for func in required_functions:
        if func not in content:
            missing.append(func)
    
    if missing:
        pytest.fail(
            f"slot_assembler.py exists but missing required functions: {missing}"
        )


def test_chapter_slot_templates_exist():

    repo_root = Path(__file__).parent.parent.parent

                    f"got {len(variants)}"

def assemble_chapter_slots(
    chapter_id: int,
    chapter_template: ChapterSlotTemplate,
    book_seed: int,
) -> ChapterAssemblyResult:
    slots_out = []

    for slot in chapter_template.slots:   # EXACTLY 10, fixed order
        variant_idx = choose_variant(
            slot_id=slot.slot_id,
            chapter_id=chapter_id,
            seed=book_seed,
        )

        try:
            variant = slot.variants[variant_idx]
        except IndexError:
            raise SlotAssemblyError(
                f"Missing variant {variant_idx} for {slot.slot_id}"

            slot_id=slot.slot_id,

            "slot_id": slot.slot_id,

            "variant_id": variant.id,
            "content_ref": rendered.ref,
        })

        chapter=chapter_id,
        slots=slots_out,
    )

## Non-Negotiable Shape

If the implementation is **real**, the assembler will look **boringly simple**.

### Core Function Signature

python
def assemble_chapter_slots(
    chapter_id: int,
    chapter_template: ChapterSlotTemplate,
    book_seed: int,
) -> ChapterAssemblyResult:
    """
    Assemble chapter using slot-based architecture.
    
    Process:
    1. Iterate through exactly 10 slots in fixed order
    2. For each slot, deterministically select variant (0-4)
    3. Render slot content
    4. If any slot fails → hard abort
    
    Returns:
        ChapterAssemblyResult with slots list
    """
    slots_out = []

    # EXACTLY 10 slots, fixed order (sorted by position)
    for slot in sorted(chapter_template.slots, key=lambda s: s.position):
        
        # Deterministic variant selection
        variant_idx = choose_variant(
            slot_id=slot.slot_id,
            chapter_id=chapter_id,
            seed=book_seed,
        )
        
        # Verify variant exists
        if variant_idx < 0 or variant_idx >= len(slot.variants):
            raise SlotAssemblyError(
                f"Invalid variant index {variant_idx} for {slot.slot_id}. "
                f"Must be 0-4, got {variant_idx}"
            )
        
        variant = slot.variants[variant_idx]
        
        # Render slot content
        rendered = render_slot_content(
            slot_id=slot.slot_id,
            variant=variant,
            chapter_id=chapter_id,
        )
        
        # Record selection (for debug artifact)
        slots_out.append({
            "slot_id": slot.slot_id,
            "variant_index": variant_idx,
            "variant_id": variant,
            "content_ref": rendered.ref,
        })

    return ChapterAssemblyResult(
        chapter=chapter_id,
        slots=slots_out,
    )

### Variant Selection (Deterministic)

python
def choose_variant(
    slot_id: str,
    chapter_id: int,
    seed: int,
) -> int:
    """
    Deterministically select variant index (0-4) for a slot.
    
    Same inputs → same output.
    No randomness. No heuristics.
    """
    # Create deterministic hash
    hash_input = f"{seed}:{chapter_id}:{slot_id}"
    hash_value = hash(hash_input)
    
    # Return index 0-4
    return abs(hash_value) % 5

**Key Properties:**
- Same seed + chapter_id + slot_id = same variant index
- Returns integer 0-4 (not variant name)
- No external dependencies
- No randomness
- No style balancing
- No arc filtering

## Red Flags (Instant Rejection)

If you see **any** of these patterns in the assembler code, it's fake or drifted:

### ❌ Banned Patterns

python
# ❌ Pool selection

    if section.role == "HOOK":
        ...

# ❌ Fallback logic

    try:
        variant = fallback_variant
    except:
        ...

# ❌ Validator-driven recovery
